The HCM is responsible for HTTP protocol handling, stream lifecycle management, filter chain execution, and connection-level decisions. Most critical gaps center on:\n\n1. **Premature Reset Detection & Draining**: Connection draining triggered by excessive premature stream resets\n2. **Deferred Request Processing**: I/O cycle-based request deferral mechanism\n3. **Codec Error & Overload Handling**: Protocol error and overload-induced connection closure\n4. **Soft HTTP/1 Draining**: Connection duration limits with HTTP/1-specific behavior\n5. **Stream Destruction Edge Cases**: Zombie stream handling and stream finalization\n6. **Header & Trailer Validation Failures**: Protocol validation with various error paths\n7. **Scoped Route Configuration Handling**: Dynamic route selection based on headers\n8. **Drain-on-Completion Interactions**: Complex state machine around connection lifecycle\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Premature Stream Reset Detection & Connection Draining\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~677-749 (functions `isPrematureRstStream`, `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`)\n**Risk**: HIGH\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nThe HCM tracks premature stream resets (streams that close without receiving upstream responses before a configured lifetime threshold). When the percentage of premature resets exceeds a configured limit across total stream count, the connection is closed via GOAWAY. This is critical infrastructure for preventing connection storms and cascading failures.\n\nTwo key functions:\n- `isPrematureRstStream()` (line 677): Determines if a closed stream should be counted as prematurely reset by comparing stream lifetime against a runtime-configurable threshold\n- `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` (line 702): Implements the detection algorithm using two criteria: (1) if premature resets exceed 50% of total requests or (2) if even assuming 100% of remaining requests are good, the threshold would still be exceeded\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No tests exist for this logic.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, DrainConnectionOnExcessivePrematureResets)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure runtime key `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds` to 1 second\n  - Configure runtime key `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count` to 10\n  - Set up connection manager to create multiple streams\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Create 10 streams with rapid creation and closure\n  2. Ensure streams close before receiving any response and within 1 second lifetime\n  3. Verify that on the 6th+ stream closure (>50% ratio), the connection transitions to `DrainState::Closing`\n  4. Verify `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` stat increments\n  5. Verify GOAWAY is sent to client\n- **Assertions**:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.value() == 1`\n  - Connection is marked for closure\n  - No further requests are accepted\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nA bug in this logic could cause either (a) connections to remain open despite DDoS-like patterns of premature resets, leading to resource exhaustion, or (b) legitimate connections to be prematurely terminated if the thresholds are miscalculated, causing availability issues. The recursion guard (`drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag) is particularly critical to prevent stack overflow.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Deferred Request Processing During High I/O Load\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~2565-2604 (functions `shouldDeferRequestProxyingToNextIoCycle`, `ActiveStream::onDeferredRequestProcessing`, `ConnectionManagerImpl::onDeferredRequestProcessing`)\n**Risk**: HIGH\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nWhen the runtime key `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle` is configured (not UINT32_MAX), the HCM defers processing of requests beyond the limit until the next I/O iteration. This prevents a single I/O event from consuming all dispatcher cycles, improving responsiveness for other connections.\n\nThree key mechanisms:\n- `shouldDeferRequestProxyingToNextIoCycle()` (line 2565): Determines if current request should be deferred based on request count and existing deferred queue\n- `ActiveStream::onDeferredRequestProcessing()` (line 2533): Processes a deferred request at next I/O iteration, reconstructing the full request (headers + data + trailers)\n- `ConnectionManagerImpl::onDeferredRequestProcessing()` (line 2583): Coordinates processing of multiple deferred streams, itself respecting the per-cycle limit\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No tests exist for deferred processing logic.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, DeferRequestProcessingWhenExceedsPerIoCycleLimit)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle` to 2 via runtime\n  - Use custom dispatcher that allows manual scheduling control\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Inject 5 pipelined HTTP/1.1 requests in single `onData()` call\n  2. Verify first 2 requests are processed immediately (headers sent to filters)\n  3. Verify next 3 requests are deferred (not sent to filters yet)\n  4. Verify `deferred_request_processing_callback_` is scheduled\n  5. Simulate callback execution (next I/O iteration)\n  6. Verify requests 3-4 are now processed (respecting limit again)\n  7. Verify request 5 is still deferred\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Request 1-2: `decodeHeaders()` called immediately\n  - Request 3-5: `decodeHeaders()` NOT called until deferred processing\n  - After deferred processing: requests 3-4 processed, request 5 still deferred\n  - Multiple I/O cycles respected: only 2 requests per iteration\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nA bug in this logic could cause either (a) starvation where deferred requests are never processed (the iteration counter could get stuck), or (b) all requests to bypass the limit by never deferring, causing a single connection to monopolize the event loop. The metadata queue handling and trailer reconstruction are particularly complex and error-prone.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Connection Closure on Codec Errors During Stream Creation\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~463-511 (functions `handleCodecError`, `handleCodecOverloadError`, `handleCodecErrorImpl`)\n**Risk**: HIGH\n**Status**: Partially tested\n\n**Description**:\nWhen the codec layer encounters protocol errors (e.g., buffer floods, invalid frames) or overload conditions during `dispatch()`, the HCM must close the connection. The logic differs between:\n- Protocol errors: increment `downstream_cx_protocol_error_`, flush write buffer, delay close\n- Overload errors: increment `downstream_rq_overload_close_`, same close type\n- Pre-codec creation overload: close before codec exists (no codec state to worry about)\n\nThe `handleCodecErrorImpl()` (line 463) consolidates closure logic but the error response flag and details string differ by error type.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: Tests exist for some codec error cases (e.g., basic protocol error) but not all combinations.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, CodecOverloadErrorBeforeCodecCreation)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Mock overload manager to report `shouldShedLoad()` == true on HCM codec creation check\n  - Configure codec factory to never be called\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Call `onData()` on connection manager without existing codec\n  2. Verify `shouldShedLoad()` check is performed on `hcm_ondata_creating_codec_` load shed point\n  3. Verify codec is NOT created\n  4. Verify connection is closed with type `FlushWriteAndDelay`\n  5. Verify response flag set appropriately\n- **Assertions**:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_overload_close_.value() == 1`\n  - `codec_` remains null\n  - `doConnectionClose()` was called exactly once\n  - Connection's response flag includes `OverloadManager`\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nThe pre-codec-creation overload path is a critical fail-safe when the system is under extreme pressure (memory allocation, etc.). If this path fails, it could allow malicious or misbehaving clients to force codec creation even under severe resource pressure, exacerbating outages.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: Soft HTTP/1 Drain on Max Connection Duration\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~769-788 (function `onConnectionDurationTimeout`)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nWhen `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` is configured and the max connection duration timer fires on an HTTP/1.1 connection, the HCM enters \"soft drain\" mode rather than full drain sequence. In soft drain:\n- No new requests are accepted (new streams set `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion` flag)\n- Existing in-flight requests complete normally\n- Connection closes after current request finishes\n\nThis is HTTP/1-specific because HTTP/2 uses GOAWAY which is safer for multiplexed scenarios.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No tests for soft drain path.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, SoftDrainHttp1OnMaxConnectionDuration)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure codec as HTTP/1.1\n  - Set `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` to true in config\n  - Set `maxConnectionDuration()` to short timeout (10ms)\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Create connection manager and simulate initial request processing\n  2. Wait for connection duration timer to fire\n  3. Simulate `onConnectionDurationTimeout()` callback\n  4. Create new stream (should be marked for drain-on-completion)\n  5. Verify drain state is NOT set to `Draining` (soft drain, not full sequence)\n  6. Verify `downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_` stat increments\n- **Assertions**:\n  - `soft_drain_http1_ == true`\n  - `drain_state_ == DrainState::NotDraining` (still not full drain)\n  - New stream has `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion() == true`\n  - For HTTP/2, verify full `startDrainSequence()` is called instead\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nIncorrect soft drain handling could cause either (a) new requests to be accepted when they shouldn't (connection stays open longer than configured), or (b) in-flight requests to be abruptly terminated (treating soft drain as hard drain on HTTP/1).\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Stream Destruction with Zombie Stream Handling\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~321-392 (function `doDeferredStreamDestroy`)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Partially tested\n\n**Description**:\nStream destruction is complex because the codec layer may still hold references to the stream object even after HCM processing is complete. The `doDeferredStreamDestroy()` function:\n1. Counts non-internally-destroyed requests for premature reset detection\n2. Disables all stream timers (idle, duration, header, access log flush)\n3. Checks if stream can be destroyed (via `canDestroyStream()`)\n4. If NOT ready: marks stream as zombie and returns (codec still has callbacks registered)\n5. If ready: logs, destroys filters, removes from stream list, potentially triggers drain sequence\n\nThe zombie stream state is critical because:\n- Zombies must not receive further data (codec might send reset/completion callbacks)\n- Zombies must be finalized when codec is done (via codec event callback)\n- Multiple timers must be cleaned up to prevent use-after-free\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: Basic stream destruction is tested but zombie stream path is not explicitly tested.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, StreamBecomesZombieWhenCodecStillActive)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Create mock codec stream that remains \"active\" (doesn't call codec complete)\n  - Use response encoder that returns false for `canDestroyStream()`\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Create stream and send request through filter chain\n  2. Send response through filter chain\n  3. Call `doDeferredStreamDestroy()` while codec is still active\n  4. Verify stream is NOT removed from `streams_` list\n  5. Verify stream is marked as zombie (`is_zombie_stream_ == true`)\n  6. Verify timers are still cleaned up\n  7. Later simulate codec completion callback\n  8. Verify stream is finally destroyed\n- **Assertions**:\n  - After first destroy: `is_zombie_stream_ == true`, still in streams list\n  - Timers (idle, duration, header, access log) all disabled\n  - Stream not in deferred delete queue\n  - After codec callback: stream finally destroyed, removed from list\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nZombie stream handling prevents use-after-free bugs. If destroyed too early, codec callbacks would access freed memory. If not destroyed when codec finishes, streams leak. The logic for determining when to destroy vs. zombie is subtle and spans HCM + codec boundary.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 6: Trailer Validation Failures with Protocol-Specific Error Handling\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1256-1300 (function `validateTrailers`)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nThe `validateTrailers()` function validates request trailers using the header validator. Validation failures trigger protocol-error-specific responses:\n- **HTTP/1**: Send 400 Bad Request to client\n- **HTTP/2+**: Reset stream instead (consistent with codec behavior)\n- **Special case**: HTTP/2 headers with underscores → reset stream (not 400)\n- **gRPC requests**: Use `Internal` gRPC status instead of plain HTTP 400\n\nThis creates 4+ code paths that must be tested independently.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No tests for trailer validation failures.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, TrailerValidationFailedHttp2ResetsStream)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Use HTTP/2 codec\n  - Configure header validator to reject trailers with status `\"invalid_trailers\"`\n  - Mock response encoder to track `resetStream()` calls\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Send request headers (valid)\n  2. Send data body\n  3. Send invalid trailers (e.g., underscore in header name: `_custom_header`)\n  4. Call `decodeTrailers()` on stream\n  5. Verify validation fails\n  6. Verify `resetStream(StreamResetReason::ProtocolError)` is called (not local reply)\n  7. Verify `downstream_cx_protocol_error_` stat or similar is incremented\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Response encoder's `resetStream()` called with `ProtocolError` reason\n  - NO `encodeHeaders()` call with 400 response\n  - `filter_manager_.streamInfo().responseFlag()` includes `DownstreamProtocolError`\n\n**Alternative Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, TrailerValidationFailedHttp1SendsBadRequest)`\n- **Setup**: Same as above but with HTTP/1.1 codec\n- **Expected**: `encodeHeaders()` called with 400 response instead of reset\n- **Assertions**: `sendLocalReply()` invoked with `BadRequest`, no stream reset\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nIncorrect trailer handling can cause protocol violations: sending a 400 on HTTP/2 when only reset is valid wastes bandwidth and confuses clients. Conversely, resetting on HTTP/1 without a response leaves the client hanging.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 7: Scoped Route Configuration Selection During Header Errors\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1361-1372 (scoped routes logic in `decodeHeaders`)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nWhen header validation or normalization fails early in `decodeHeaders()`, the code must still have selected a route configuration (for scope key computation). The logic:\n1. Checks if routing is enabled (`config_->isRoutable()`)\n2. If yes: either gets route config provider OR gets scoped route config provider + scope builder\n3. For scoped routes: calls `snapScopedRouteConfig()` which calls `scopeKeyBuilder()->computeScopeKey(*request_headers_)` using UNVALIDATED headers\n4. If scope key is invalid (e.g., contains invalid characters), `getRouteConfig()` returns null and fallback to `NullConfigImpl()`\n\nThe issue: if header validation fails (e.g., underscore in header name), the scope key computation may have consumed invalid header data, or the key computation itself may fail.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: Scoped routes are tested but not with header validation failures.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, ScopedRouteConfigWithInvalidHeaderInScopeKey)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure scoped routes with scope key builder that uses custom header (e.g., `x-my-scope`)\n  - Configure header validator to reject headers with underscores\n  - Set up mock scoped route config provider\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Send request with invalid header that would be used for scope key\n  2. Verify scope key computation still happens (before validation)\n  3. Verify if scope key builder raises error, fallback to `NullConfigImpl()` occurs\n  4. Verify header validation still fails and sends error response\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Route config is set (either valid or null fallback)\n  - Validation error response sent (400 Bad Request)\n  - No crash or double-processing\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nA bug could cause (a) scope key computation to fail and hang the request, or (b) invalid headers to be used in routing decisions if validation order is wrong. This affects correctness of routing and header security.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 8: Drain-on-Completion Interaction During Overload Response\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1907-1961 (overload handling in `encodeHeaders`)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Partially tested\n\n**Description**:\nThe `encodeHeaders()` function implements complex state machine:\n1. Check if connection should drain due to overload (random Bernoulli trial)\n2. If yes AND not already draining: start drain sequence, increment stat\n3. Check if stream set `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion`\n4. If yes AND not draining: start drain sequence OR set drain state based on protocol\n5. Check if incomplete request (remote not done) + non-multiplexing codec: set drain state\n\nThe issue: multiple conditions can trigger drain actions. If both overload AND shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion are true, the logic must handle this correctly without double-starting the drain sequence.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: Drain-on-completion is tested but not in combination with overload.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, OverloadDrainAndStreamDrainBothTriggered)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure overload manager to return true for `DisableHttpKeepAlive` override\n  - Mock Bernoulli random number to return true\n  - Use HTTP/2 codec\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Incorrect interaction could cause drain to be silently skipped if one condition is checked after the state is already modified.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 9: CONNECT-UDP Request Rewriting Failure Handling\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1445-1450 (CONNECT-UDP validation)\n**Risk**: LOW\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nCONNECT-UDP is an HTTP extension (RFC 9298) for proxying UDP. The code:\n```cpp\nif (HeaderUtility::isConnectUdpRequest(*request_headers_) &&\n    !HeaderUtility::rewriteAuthorityForConnectUdp(*request_headers_)) {\n  sendLocalReply(Code::NotFound, \"The path is incorrect for CONNECT-UDP\", ...);\n  return;\n}\n```\n\nThis checks if the request is CONNECT-UDP and if the authority rewriting succeeds. Rewriting can fail if the path format is invalid (e.g., malformed `?connect-udp` parameter). The current code sends a 404 with specific message. However:\n- This code path is rarely hit because CONNECT-UDP is still experimental\n- The error message is user-facing, so wrong messages could confuse clients\n- The test would ensure the rewrite function is correctly integrated\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No specific tests for CONNECT-UDP rewrite failures.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, ConnectUdpRewriteFailureReturns404)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Prepare request with method \"CONNECT\" and query string \"?connect-udp\" but invalid format\n  - Mock `HeaderUtility::rewriteAuthorityForConnectUdp()` to return false\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. If the error check is broken, malformed CONNECT-UDP requests might be passed to the router and fail there (wrong error message).\n\n---\n\n### Gap 10: Header Validation Redirect vs. Reject Decision Making\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1197-1254 (function `validateHeaders` with redirect logic)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nThe `validateHeaders()` function handles both validation and transformation of request headers. The stat charging is also important for monitoring and debugging.\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\n### Primary Source Files Analyzed\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (~2,600 lines) — Main HCM implementation\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` — HCM interface and inner class definitions\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` — Filter chain execution logic\n- `source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` — Header manipulation utilities\n\n### Primary Test Files\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc` — Main HCM unit tests (~5,000 lines)\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc` — Additional HCM tests\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_3.cc` — Additional HCM tests\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.h/cc` — Test infrastructure and fixtures\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_misc_test.cc` — Miscellaneous HCM tests\n- `test/common/http/filter_manager_test.cc` — Filter manager tests\n\n### Key Runtime Keys Involved\n- `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count` (default: 500)\n- `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds` (default: 1)\n- `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle` (default: UINT32_MAX)\n- `http1.optionally_delay_close`\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.reset_with_error`\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.trace_refresh_after_route_refresh`\n- Various header-related overrides\n\n---\n\n## Recommendations\n\n### Priority 1 (Critical - The HCM is responsible for HTTP protocol handling, stream lifecycle management, filter chain execution, and connection-level decisions. Most critical gaps center on:\n\n1. **Premature Reset Detection & Draining**: Connection draining triggered by excessive premature stream resets\n2. **Deferred Request Processing**: I/O cycle-based request deferral mechanism\n3. **Codec Error & Overload Handling**: Protocol error and overload-induced connection closure\n4. **Soft HTTP/1 Draining**: Connection duration limits with HTTP/1-specific behavior\n5. **Stream Destruction Edge Cases**: Zombie stream handling and stream finalization\n6. **Header & Trailer Validation Failures**: Protocol validation with various error paths\n7. **Scoped Route Configuration Handling**: Dynamic route selection based on headers\n8. **Drain-on-Completion Interactions**: Complex state machine around connection lifecycle\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Premature Stream Reset Detection & Connection Draining\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~677-749 (functions `isPrematureRstStream`, `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`)\n**Risk**: HIGH\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nThe HCM tracks premature stream resets (streams that close without receiving upstream responses before a configured lifetime threshold). When the percentage of premature resets exceeds a configured limit across total stream count, the connection is closed via GOAWAY. This is critical infrastructure for preventing connection storms and cascading failures.\n\nTwo key functions:\n- `isPrematureRstStream()` (line 677): Determines if a closed stream should be counted as prematurely reset by comparing stream lifetime against a runtime-configurable threshold\n- `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` (line 702): Implements the detection algorithm using two criteria: (1) if premature resets exceed 50% of total requests or (2) if even assuming 100% of remaining requests are good, the threshold would still be exceeded\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No tests exist for this logic.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, DrainConnectionOnExcessivePrematureResets)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure runtime key `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds` to 1 second\n  - Configure runtime key `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count` to 10\n  - Set up connection manager to create multiple streams\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Create 10 streams with rapid creation and closure\n  2. Ensure streams close before receiving any response and within 1 second lifetime\n  3. Verify that on the 6th+ stream closure (>50% ratio), the connection transitions to `DrainState::Closing`\n  4. Verify `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` stat increments\n  5. Verify GOAWAY is sent to client\n- **Assertions**:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.value() == 1`\n  - Connection is marked for closure\n  - No further requests are accepted\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nA bug in this logic could cause either (a) connections to remain open despite DDoS-like patterns of premature resets, leading to resource exhaustion, or (b) legitimate connections to be prematurely terminated if the thresholds are miscalculated, causing availability issues. The recursion guard (`drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag) is particularly critical to prevent stack overflow.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Deferred Request Processing During High I/O Load\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~2565-2604 (functions `shouldDeferRequestProxyingToNextIoCycle`, `ActiveStream::onDeferredRequestProcessing`, `ConnectionManagerImpl::onDeferredRequestProcessing`)\n**Risk**: HIGH\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nWhen the runtime key `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle` is configured (not UINT32_MAX), the HCM defers processing of requests beyond the limit until the next I/O iteration. This prevents a single I/O event from consuming all dispatcher cycles, improving responsiveness for other connections.\n\nThree key mechanisms:\n- `shouldDeferRequestProxyingToNextIoCycle()` (line 2565): Determines if current request should be deferred based on request count and existing deferred queue\n- `ActiveStream::onDeferredRequestProcessing()` (line 2533): Processes a deferred request at next I/O iteration, reconstructing the full request (headers + data + trailers)\n- `ConnectionManagerImpl::onDeferredRequestProcessing()` (line 2583): Coordinates processing of multiple deferred streams, itself respecting the per-cycle limit\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No tests exist for deferred processing logic.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, DeferRequestProcessingWhenExceedsPerIoCycleLimit)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle` to 2 via runtime\n  - Use custom dispatcher that allows manual scheduling control\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Inject 5 pipelined HTTP/1.1 requests in single `onData()` call\n  2. Verify first 2 requests are processed immediately (headers sent to filters)\n  3. Verify next 3 requests are deferred (not sent to filters yet)\n  4. Verify `deferred_request_processing_callback_` is scheduled\n  5. Simulate callback execution (next I/O iteration)\n  6. Verify requests 3-4 are now processed (respecting limit again)\n  7. Verify request 5 is still deferred\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Request 1-2: `decodeHeaders()` called immediately\n  - Request 3-5: `decodeHeaders()` NOT called until deferred processing\n  - After deferred processing: requests 3-4 processed, request 5 still deferred\n  - Multiple I/O cycles respected: only 2 requests per iteration\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nA bug in this logic could cause either (a) starvation where deferred requests are never processed (the iteration counter could get stuck), or (b) all requests to bypass the limit by never deferring, causing a single connection to monopolize the event loop. The metadata queue handling and trailer reconstruction are particularly complex and error-prone.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Connection Closure on Codec Errors During Stream Creation\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~463-511 (functions `handleCodecError`, `handleCodecOverloadError`, `handleCodecErrorImpl`)\n**Risk**: HIGH\n**Status**: Partially tested\n\n**Description**:\nWhen the codec layer encounters protocol errors (e.g., buffer floods, invalid frames) or overload conditions during `dispatch()`, the HCM must close the connection. The logic differs between:\n- Protocol errors: increment `downstream_cx_protocol_error_`, flush write buffer, delay close\n- Overload errors: increment `downstream_rq_overload_close_`, same close type\n- Pre-codec creation overload: close before codec exists (no codec state to worry about)\n\nThe `handleCodecErrorImpl()` (line 463) consolidates closure logic but the error response flag and details string differ by error type.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: Tests exist for some codec error cases (e.g., basic protocol error) but not all combinations.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, CodecOverloadErrorBeforeCodecCreation)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Mock overload manager to report `shouldShedLoad()` == true on HCM codec creation check\n  - Configure codec factory to never be called\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Call `onData()` on connection manager without existing codec\n  2. Verify `shouldShedLoad()` check is performed on `hcm_ondata_creating_codec_` load shed point\n  3. Verify codec is NOT created\n  4. Verify connection is closed with type `FlushWriteAndDelay`\n  5. Verify response flag set appropriately\n- **Assertions**:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_overload_close_.value() == 1`\n  - `codec_` remains null\n  - `doConnectionClose()` was called exactly once\n  - Connection's response flag includes `OverloadManager`\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nThe pre-codec-creation overload path is a critical fail-safe when the system is under extreme pressure (memory allocation, etc.). If this path fails, it could allow malicious or misbehaving clients to force codec creation even under severe resource pressure, exacerbating outages.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: Soft HTTP/1 Drain on Max Connection Duration\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~769-788 (function `onConnectionDurationTimeout`)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nWhen `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` is configured and the max connection duration timer fires on an HTTP/1.1 connection, the HCM enters \"soft drain\" mode rather than full drain sequence. In soft drain:\n- No new requests are accepted (new streams set `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion` flag)\n- Existing in-flight requests complete normally\n- Connection closes after current request finishes\n\nThis is HTTP/1-specific because HTTP/2 uses GOAWAY which is safer for multiplexed scenarios.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No tests for soft drain path.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, SoftDrainHttp1OnMaxConnectionDuration)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure codec as HTTP/1.1\n  - Set `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` to true in config\n  - Set `maxConnectionDuration()` to short timeout (10ms)\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Create connection manager and simulate initial request processing\n  2. Wait for connection duration timer to fire\n  3. Simulate `onConnectionDurationTimeout()` callback\n  4. Create new stream (should be marked for drain-on-completion)\n  5. Verify drain state is NOT set to `Draining` (soft drain, not full sequence)\n  6. Verify `downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_` stat increments\n- **Assertions**:\n  - `soft_drain_http1_ == true`\n  - `drain_state_ == DrainState::NotDraining` (still not full drain)\n  - New stream has `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion() == true`\n  - For HTTP/2, verify full `startDrainSequence()` is called instead\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nIncorrect soft drain handling could cause either (a) new requests to be accepted when they shouldn't (connection stays open longer than configured), or (b) in-flight requests to be abruptly terminated (treating soft drain as hard drain on HTTP/1).\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Stream Destruction with Zombie Stream Handling\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~321-392 (function `doDeferredStreamDestroy`)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Partially tested\n\n**Description**:\nStream destruction is complex because the codec layer may still hold references to the stream object even after HCM processing is complete. The `doDeferredStreamDestroy()` function:\n1. Counts non-internally-destroyed requests for premature reset detection\n2. Disables all stream timers (idle, duration, header, access log flush)\n3. Checks if stream can be destroyed (via `canDestroyStream()`)\n4. If NOT ready: marks stream as zombie and returns (codec still has callbacks registered)\n5. If ready: logs, destroys filters, removes from stream list, potentially triggers drain sequence\n\nThe zombie stream state is critical because:\n- Zombies must not receive further data (codec might send reset/completion callbacks)\n- Zombies must be finalized when codec is done (via codec event callback)\n- Multiple timers must be cleaned up to prevent use-after-free\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: Basic stream destruction is tested but zombie stream path is not explicitly tested.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, StreamBecomesZombieWhenCodecStillActive)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Create mock codec stream that remains \"active\" (doesn't call codec complete)\n  - Use response encoder that returns false for `canDestroyStream()`\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Create stream and send request through filter chain\n  2. Send response through filter chain\n  3. Call `doDeferredStreamDestroy()` while codec is still active\n  4. Verify stream is NOT removed from `streams_` list\n  5. Verify stream is marked as zombie (`is_zombie_stream_ == true`)\n  6. Verify timers are still cleaned up\n  7. Later simulate codec completion callback\n  8. Verify stream is finally destroyed\n- **Assertions**:\n  - After first destroy: `is_zombie_stream_ == true`, still in streams list\n  - Timers (idle, duration, header, access log) all disabled\n  - Stream not in deferred delete queue\n  - After codec callback: stream finally destroyed, removed from list\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nZombie stream handling prevents use-after-free bugs. If destroyed too early, codec callbacks would access freed memory. If not destroyed when codec finishes, streams leak. The logic for determining when to destroy vs. zombie is subtle and spans HCM + codec boundary.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 6: Trailer Validation Failures with Protocol-Specific Error Handling\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1256-1300 (function `validateTrailers`)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nThe `validateTrailers()` function validates request trailers using the header validator. Validation failures trigger protocol-error-specific responses:\n- **HTTP/1**: Send 400 Bad Request to client\n- **HTTP/2+**: Reset stream instead (consistent with codec behavior)\n- **Special case**: HTTP/2 headers with underscores → reset stream (not 400)\n- **gRPC requests**: Use `Internal` gRPC status instead of plain HTTP 400\n\nThis creates 4+ code paths that must be tested independently.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No tests for trailer validation failures.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, TrailerValidationFailedHttp2ResetsStream)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Use HTTP/2 codec\n  - Configure header validator to reject trailers with status `\"invalid_trailers\"`\n  - Mock response encoder to track `resetStream()` calls\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Send request headers (valid)\n  2. Send data body\n  3. Send invalid trailers (e.g., underscore in header name: `_custom_header`)\n  4. Call `decodeTrailers()` on stream\n  5. Verify validation fails\n  6. Verify `resetStream(StreamResetReason::ProtocolError)` is called (not local reply)\n  7. Verify `downstream_cx_protocol_error_` stat or similar is incremented\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Response encoder's `resetStream()` called with `ProtocolError` reason\n  - NO `encodeHeaders()` call with 400 response\n  - `filter_manager_.streamInfo().responseFlag()` includes `DownstreamProtocolError`\n\n**Alternative Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, TrailerValidationFailedHttp1SendsBadRequest)`\n- **Setup**: Same as above but with HTTP/1.1 codec\n- **Expected**: `encodeHeaders()` called with 400 response instead of reset\n- **Assertions**: `sendLocalReply()` invoked with `BadRequest`, no stream reset\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nIncorrect trailer handling can cause protocol violations: sending a 400 on HTTP/2 when only reset is valid wastes bandwidth and confuses clients. Conversely, resetting on HTTP/1 without a response leaves the client hanging.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 7: Scoped Route Configuration Selection During Header Errors\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1361-1372 (scoped routes logic in `decodeHeaders`)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nWhen header validation or normalization fails early in `decodeHeaders()`, the code must still have selected a route configuration (for scope key computation). The logic:\n1. Checks if routing is enabled (`config_->isRoutable()`)\n2. If yes: either gets route config provider OR gets scoped route config provider + scope builder\n3. For scoped routes: calls `snapScopedRouteConfig()` which calls `scopeKeyBuilder()->computeScopeKey(*request_headers_)` using UNVALIDATED headers\n4. If scope key is invalid (e.g., contains invalid characters), `getRouteConfig()` returns null and fallback to `NullConfigImpl()`\n\nThe issue: if header validation fails (e.g., underscore in header name), the scope key computation may have consumed invalid header data, or the key computation itself may fail.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: Scoped routes are tested but not with header validation failures.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, ScopedRouteConfigWithInvalidHeaderInScopeKey)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure scoped routes with scope key builder that uses custom header (e.g., `x-my-scope`)\n  - Configure header validator to reject headers with underscores\n  - Set up mock scoped route config provider\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Send request with invalid header that would be used for scope key\n  2. Verify scope key computation still happens (before validation)\n  3. Verify if scope key builder raises error, fallback to `NullConfigImpl()` occurs\n  4. Verify header validation still fails and sends error response\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Route config is set (either valid or null fallback)\n  - Validation error response sent (400 Bad Request)\n  - No crash or double-processing\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nA bug could cause (a) scope key computation to fail and hang the request, or (b) invalid headers to be used in routing decisions if validation order is wrong. This affects correctness of routing and header security.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 8: Drain-on-Completion Interaction During Overload Response\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1907-1961 (overload handling in `encodeHeaders`)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Partially tested\n\n**Description**:\nThe `encodeHeaders()` function implements complex state machine:\n1. Check if connection should drain due to overload (random Bernoulli trial)\n2. If yes AND not already draining: start drain sequence, increment stat\n3. Check if stream set `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion`\n4. If yes AND not draining: start drain sequence OR set drain state based on protocol\n5. Check if incomplete request (remote not done) + non-multiplexing codec: set drain state\n\nThe issue: multiple conditions can trigger drain actions. If both overload AND shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion are true, the logic must handle this correctly without double-starting the drain sequence.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: Drain-on-completion is tested but not in combination with overload.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, OverloadDrainAndStreamDrainBothTriggered)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure overload manager to return true for `DisableHttpKeepAlive` override\n  - Mock Bernoulli random number to return true\n  - Use HTTP/2 codec\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. Verify overload drain is detected AND stream drain is set\n  5. Verify drain sequence is started only ONCE (not twice)\n  6. Verify GOAWAY is sent\n- **Assertions**:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_cx_overload_disable_keepalive_.value() == 1`\n  - Drain state transitioned once to `Draining`\n  - `startDrainSequence()` called exactly once (not twice)\n  - No error messages or crashes\n\n**Why It Matters**:\nDouble-starting the drain sequence could cause assertion failures or resource leaks (two drain timers created). Incorrect interaction could cause drain to be silently skipped if one condition is checked after the state is already modified.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 9: CONNECT-UDP Request Rewriting Failure Handling\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1445-1450 (CONNECT-UDP validation)\n**Risk**: LOW\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nCONNECT-UDP is an HTTP extension (RFC 9298) for proxying UDP. The code:\n```cpp\nif (HeaderUtility::isConnectUdpRequest(*request_headers_) &&\n    !HeaderUtility::rewriteAuthorityForConnectUdp(*request_headers_)) {\n  sendLocalReply(Code::NotFound, \"The path is incorrect for CONNECT-UDP\", ...);\n  return;\n}\n```\n\nThis checks if the request is CONNECT-UDP and if the authority rewriting succeeds. Rewriting can fail if the path format is invalid (e.g., malformed `?connect-udp` parameter). The current code sends a 404 with specific message. However:\n- This code path is rarely hit because CONNECT-UDP is still experimental\n- The error message is user-facing, so wrong messages could confuse clients\n- The test would ensure the rewrite function is correctly integrated\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No specific tests for CONNECT-UDP rewrite failures.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, ConnectUdpRewriteFailureReturns404)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Prepare request with method \"CONNECT\" and query string \"?connect-udp\" but invalid format\n  - Mock `HeaderUtility::rewriteAuthorityForConnectUdp()` to return false\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. If the error check is broken, malformed CONNECT-UDP requests might be passed to the router and fail there (wrong error message).\n\n---\n\n### Gap 10: Header Validation Redirect vs. Reject Decision Making\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1197-1254 (function `validateHeaders` with redirect logic)\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n**Status**: Not tested\n\n**Description**:\nThe `validateHeaders()` function handles both validation and transformation of request headers. The transformation result can indicate:\n- **OK**: Headers are valid\n- **Redirect**: Path was normalized and should 307 redirect (non-gRPC only)\n- **Failure**: Headers are invalid, return error\n\nThe logic:\n```cpp\nredirect = transformation_result.action() ==\n    Http::ServerHeaderValidator::RequestHeadersTransformationResult::Action::Redirect;\nif (redirect && !is_grpc) {\n  connection_manager_.stats_.named_.downstream_rq_redirected_with_normalized_path_.inc();\n} else if (failure) {\n  connection_manager_.stats_.named_.downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization_.inc();\n}\n```\n\nThis means:\n- Redirect on gRPC: treated as failure (gRPC clients don't follow redirects)\n- Redirect on HTTP: sends 307 with Location header\n- Both paths must set the response flag, details, and potentially close connection for protocol errors\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: Path normalization redirect is tested but not specifically for the header validator integration or gRPC case.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, HeaderValidationRedirectRejectedForGrpc)`\n- **Setup**:\n  - Configure header validator to return redirect action for normalized path\n  - Create request with gRPC content-type and path requiring normalization (e.g., `/foo//bar` → `/foo/bar`)\n- **Test Flow**:\n  1. The stat charging is also important for monitoring and debugging.\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\n### Primary Source Files Analyzed\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (~2,600 lines) — Main HCM implementation\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` — HCM interface and inner class definitions\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` — Filter chain execution logic\n- `source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` — Header manipulation utilities\n\n### Primary Test Files\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc` — Main HCM unit tests (~5,000 lines)\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc` — Additional HCM tests\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_3.cc` — Additional HCM tests\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.h/cc` — Test infrastructure and fixtures\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_misc_test.cc` — Miscellaneous HCM tests\n- `test/common/http/filter_manager_test.cc` — Filter manager tests\n\n### Key Runtime Keys Involved\n- `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count` (default: 500)\n- `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds` (default: 1)\n- `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle` (default: UINT32_MAX)\n- `http1.optionally_delay_close`\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.reset_with_error`\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.trace_refresh_after_route_refresh`\n- Various header-related overrides\n\n---\n\n## Recommendations\n\n### Priority 1 (Critical -
